</tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Biology deals with the study of the many living\n         <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n          organisms\n         </a>\n         .\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           top:\n           <i>\n            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/E._coli" title="E. coli">\n             E. coli\n            </a>\n           </i>\n           bacteria and\n           <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">\n            gazelle\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           bottom:\n           <a href="/wiki/Goliathus" title="Goliathus">\n            Goliath beetle\n           </a>\n           and\n           <a href="/wiki/Tree_fern" title="Tree fern">\n            tree fern\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Biology\n       </b>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">\n        natural science\n       </a>\n       that involves the study of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       and living\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organisms\n       </a>\n       , including their physical and\n       <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n        chemical structure\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">\n        function\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Developmental_biology" title="Developmental biology">\n        development\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">\n        evolution\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aquarenagloss_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-aquarenagloss-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Modern biology is a vast field, composed of many\n       <a href="#Branches">\n        branches\n       </a>\n       . Despite the broad scope and the complexity of the science, there are certain unifying concepts that consolidate it into a single, coherent field. In general, biology recognizes the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">\n        cell\n       </a>\n       as the basic unit of life,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genes" title="Genes">\n        genes\n       </a>\n       as the basic unit of\n       <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">\n        heredity\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">\n        evolution\n       </a>\n       as the engine that propels the creation of new\n       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">\n        species\n       </a>\n       . It is also understood that all organisms survive by consuming and transforming\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       and by\n       <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">\n        regulating\n       </a>\n       their internal environment.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Sub-disciplines of biology are defined by the scale at which life is studied, the kinds of organisms studied, and the methods used to study them:\n       <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n        biochemistry\n       </a>\n       examines the rudimentary chemistry of life;\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n        molecular biology\n       </a>\n       studies the complex interactions among biological\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecules\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellular_biology" title="Cellular biology">\n        cellular biology\n       </a>\n       examines the basic building-block of all life, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">\n        cell\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">\n        physiology\n       </a>\n       examines the physical and chemical functions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tissue_(biology)" title="Tissue (biology)">\n        tissues\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">\n        organs\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Organ_system" title="Organ system">\n        organ systems\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">\n        ecology\n       </a>\n       examines how organisms interact in their\n       <a href="/wiki/Environment_(biophysical)" title="Environment (biophysical)">\n        environment\n       </a>\n       ; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_biology" title="Evolutionary biology">\n        evolutionary biology\n       </a>\n       examines the processes that produced the diversity of life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_of_life_by_Haeckel.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Haeckel" title="Ernst Haeckel">\n          Ernst Haeckel\n         </a>\n         \'s Tree of Life (1879)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The term\n       <i>\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/biology" title="wikt:biology">\n         biology\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       is derived from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_Language" title="Greek Language">\n        Greek\n       </a>\n       word\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%B2%CE%AF%CE%BF%CF%82" title="wikt:\xce\xb2\xce\xaf\xce\xbf\xcf\x82">\n         \xce\xb2\xce\xaf\xce\xbf\xcf\x82\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        bios\n       </i>\n       , "\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       " and the suffix\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-%CE%BB%CE%BF%CE%B3%CE%AF%CE%B1" title="wikt:-\xce\xbb\xce\xbf\xce\xb3\xce\xaf\xce\xb1">\n         -\xce\xbb\xce\xbf\xce\xb3\xce\xaf\xce\xb1\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        -logia\n       </i>\n       , "study of."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OnlineEtDict_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OnlineEtDict-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Latin-language form of the term first appeared in 1736 when Swedish scientist\n       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">\n        Carl Linnaeus\n       </a>\n       (Carl von Linn\xc3\xa9) used\n       <i>\n        biologi\n       </i>\n       in his\n       <i>\n        Bibliotheca botanica\n       </i>\n       . It was used again in 1766 in a work entitled\n       <i>\n        Philosophiae naturalis sive physicae: tomus III, continens geologian, biologian, phytologian generalis\n       </i>\n       , by\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Christoph_Hanow" title="Michael Christoph Hanow">\n        Michael Christoph Hanov\n       </a>\n       , a disciple of\n       <a href="/wiki/Christian_Wolff_(philosopher)" title="Christian Wolff (philosopher)">\n        Christian Wolff\n       </a>\n       . The first German use,\n       <i>\n        Biologie\n       </i>\n       , was in a 1771 translation of Linnaeus\' work. In 1797, Theodor Georg August Roose used the term in the preface of a book,\n       <i>\n        Grundz\xc3\xbcge der Lehre van der Lebenskraft\n       </i>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich_Burdach" title="Karl Friedrich Burdach">\n        Karl Friedrich Burdach\n       </a>\n       used the term in 1800 in a more restricted sense of the study of human beings from a morphological, physiological and psychological perspective (\n       <i>\n        Prop\xc3\xa4deutik zum Studien der gesammten Heilkunst\n       </i>\n       ). The term came into its modern usage with the six-volume treatise\n       <i>\n        Biologie, oder Philosophie der lebenden Natur\n       </i>\n       (1802\xe2\x80\x9322) by\n       <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_Reinhold_Treviranus" title="Gottfried Reinhold Treviranus">\n        Gottfried Reinhold Treviranus\n       </a>\n       , who announced:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Richards_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Richards-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        The objects of our research will be the different forms and manifestations of life, the conditions and laws under which these phenomena occur, and the causes through which they have been effected. The science that concerns itself with these objects we will indicate by the name biology [Biologie] or the doctrine of life [Lebenslehre].\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Although modern biology is a relatively recent development, sciences related to and included within it have been studied since ancient times.\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_philosophy" title="Natural philosophy">\n        Natural philosophy\n       </a>\n       was studied as early as the ancient civilizations of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">\n        Mesopotamia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">\n        Egypt\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">\n        Indian subcontinent\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">\n        China\n       </a>\n       . However, the origins of modern biology and its approach to the study of nature are most often traced back to\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">\n        ancient Greece\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While the formal study of\n       <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">\n        medicine\n       </a>\n       dates back to\n       <a href="/wiki/Hippocrates" title="Hippocrates">\n        Hippocrates\n       </a>\n       (ca. 460 BC \xe2\x80\x93 ca. 370 BC), it was\n       <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">\n        Aristotle\n       </a>\n       (384 BC \xe2\x80\x93 322 BC) who contributed most extensively to the development of biology. Especially important are his\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Animals" title="History of Animals">\n        History of Animals\n       </a>\n       and other works where he showed naturalist leanings, and later more empirical works that focused on biological causation and the diversity of life. Aristotle\'s successor at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lyceum" title="Lyceum">\n        Lyceum\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Theophrastus" title="Theophrastus">\n        Theophrastus\n       </a>\n       , wrote a series of books on\n       <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">\n        botany\n       </a>\n       that survived as the most important contribution of antiquity to the plant sciences, even into the\n       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">\n        Middle Ages\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eb1911_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eb1911-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Scholars of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Science_in_the_medieval_Islamic_world" title="Science in the medieval Islamic world">\n        medieval Islamic world\n       </a>\n       who wrote on biology included\n       <a href="/wiki/Al-Jahiz" title="Al-Jahiz">\n        al-Jahiz\n       </a>\n       (781\xe2\x80\x93869),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Al-D%C4%ABnawar%C4%AB" title="Al-D\xc4\xabnawar\xc4\xab">\n        Al-D\xc4\xabnawar\xc4\xab\n       </a>\n       (828\xe2\x80\x93896), who wrote on botany,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahd-815_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Fahd-815-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Zakar%C4%ABya_R%C4%81zi" title="Muhammad ibn Zakar\xc4\xabya R\xc4\x81zi">\n        Rhazes\n       </a>\n       (865\xe2\x80\x93925) who wrote on\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">\n        anatomy\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">\n        physiology\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">\n        Medicine\n       </a>\n       was especially well studied by Islamic scholars working in Greek philosopher traditions, while natural history drew heavily on Aristotelian thought, especially in upholding a fixed hierarchy of life.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Biology began to quickly develop and grow with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anton_van_Leeuwenhoek" title="Anton van Leeuwenhoek">\n        Anton van Leeuwenhoek\n       </a>\n       \'s dramatic improvement of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">\n        microscope\n       </a>\n       . It was then that scholars discovered\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spermatozoa" title="Spermatozoa">\n        spermatozoa\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">\n        bacteria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Infusoria" title="Infusoria">\n        infusoria\n       </a>\n       and the diversity of microscopic life. Investigations by\n       <a href="/wiki/Jan_Swammerdam" title="Jan Swammerdam">\n        Jan Swammerdam\n       </a>\n       led to new interest in\n       <a href="/wiki/Entomology" title="Entomology">\n        entomology\n       </a>\n       and helped to develop the basic techniques of microscopic\n       <a href="/wiki/Dissection" title="Dissection">\n        dissection\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Staining" title="Staining">\n        staining\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Advances in\n       <a href="/wiki/Microscopy" title="Microscopy">\n        microscopy\n       </a>\n       also had a profound impact on biological thinking. In the early 19th century, a number of biologists pointed to the central importance of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">\n        cell\n       </a>\n       . Then, in 1838,\n       <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Jakob_Schleiden" title="Matthias Jakob Schleiden">\n        Schleiden\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Schwann" title="Theodor Schwann">\n        Schwann\n       </a>\n       began promoting the now universal ideas that (1) the basic unit of organisms is the cell and (2) that individual cells have all the characteristics of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       , although they opposed the idea that (3) all cells come from the division of other cells. Thanks to the work of\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Remak" title="Robert Remak">\n        Robert Remak\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Virchow" title="Rudolf Virchow">\n        Rudolf Virchow\n       </a>\n       , however, by the 1860s most biologists accepted all three tenets of what came to be known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_theory" title="Cell theory">\n        cell theory\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Meanwhile, taxonomy and classification became the focus of natural historians.\n       <a href="/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus" title="Carl Linnaeus">\n        Carl Linnaeus\n       </a>\n       published a basic\n       <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)" title="Taxonomy (biology)">\n        taxonomy\n       </a>\n       for the natural world in 1735 (variations of which have been in use ever since), and in the 1750s introduced\n       <a href="/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature" title="Binomial nomenclature">\n        scientific names\n       </a>\n       for all his species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Georges-Louis_Leclerc,_Comte_de_Buffon" title="Georges-Louis Leclerc, Comte de Buffon">\n        Georges-Louis Leclerc, Comte de Buffon\n       </a>\n       , treated species as artificial categories and living forms as malleable\xe2\x80\x94even suggesting the possibility of\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_descent" title="Common descent">\n        common descent\n       </a>\n       . Though he was opposed to evolution, Buffon is a key figure in the\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_evolutionary_thought" title="History of evolutionary thought">\n        history of evolutionary thought\n       </a>\n       ; his work influenced the evolutionary theories of both\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lamarck" title="Lamarck">\n        Lamarck\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">\n        Darwin\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Serious evolutionary thinking originated with the works of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Lamarck" title="Jean-Baptiste Lamarck">\n        Jean-Baptiste Lamarck\n       </a>\n       , who was the first to present a coherent theory of evolution.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gould_2002_187_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gould_2002_187-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He posited that evolution was the result of environmental stress on properties of animals, meaning that the more frequently and rigorously an organ was used, the more complex and efficient it would become, thus adapting the animal to its environment. Lamarck believed that these acquired traits could then be passed on to the animal\'s offspring, who would further develop and perfect them.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lam1914_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Lam1914-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, it was the British naturalist\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">\n        Charles Darwin\n       </a>\n       , combining the biogeographical approach of\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">\n        Humboldt\n       </a>\n       , the uniformitarian geology of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lyell" title="Charles Lyell">\n        Lyell\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Malthus" title="Thomas Malthus">\n        Malthus\'s\n       </a>\n       writings on population growth, and his own morphological expertise and extensive natural observations, who forged a more successful evolutionary theory based on\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">\n        natural selection\n       </a>\n       ; similar reasoning and evidence led\n       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Russel_Wallace" title="Alfred Russel Wallace">\n        Alfred Russel Wallace\n       </a>\n       to independently reach the same conclusions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although it was the subject of\n       <a href="/wiki/Creation%E2%80%93evolution_controversy" title="Creation\xe2\x80\x93evolution controversy">\n        controversy\n       </a>\n       (which continues to this day), Darwin\'s theory quickly spread through the scientific community and soon became a central axiom of the rapidly developing science of biology.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The discovery of the physical representation of heredity came along with evolutionary principles and\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_genetics" title="Population genetics">\n        population genetics\n       </a>\n       . In the 1940s and early 1950s, experiments pointed to\n       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">\n        DNA\n       </a>\n       as the component of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chromosomes" title="Chromosomes">\n        chromosomes\n       </a>\n       that held the trait-carrying units that had become known as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genes" title="Genes">\n        genes\n       </a>\n       . A focus on new kinds of model organisms such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viruses" title="Viruses">\n        viruses\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">\n        bacteria\n       </a>\n       , along with the discovery of the double helical structure of DNA in 1953, marked the transition to the era of\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_genetics" title="Molecular genetics">\n        molecular genetics\n       </a>\n       . From the 1950s to present times, biology has been vastly extended in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molecular_Biology" title="Molecular Biology">\n        molecular\n       </a>\n       domain. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetic_code" title="Genetic code">\n        genetic code\n       </a>\n       was cracked by\n       <a href="/wiki/Har_Gobind_Khorana" title="Har Gobind Khorana">\n        Har Gobind Khorana\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_W._Holley" title="Robert W. Holley">\n        Robert W. Holley\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Warren_Nirenberg" title="Marshall Warren Nirenberg">\n        Marshall Warren Nirenberg\n       </a>\n       after DNA was understood to contain\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Codons" title="Codons">\n        codons\n       </a>\n       . Finally, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_Genome_Project" title="Human Genome Project">\n        Human Genome Project\n       </a>\n       was launched in 1990 with the goal of mapping the general human\n       <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">\n        genome\n       </a>\n       . This project was essentially completed in 2003,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with further analysis still being published. The Human Genome Project was the first step in a globalized effort to incorporate accumulated knowledge of biology into a functional, molecular definition of the human body and the bodies of other organisms.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foundations_of_modern_biology">\n        Foundations of modern biology\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cell_theory">\n        Cell theory\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg">\n         <img alt="HeLa cells stained with Hoechst blue stain." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="459" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg/250px-HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg/375px-HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6c/HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HeLa_cells_stained_with_Hoechst_33258.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Human\n         <a href="/wiki/Cancer_cell" title="Cancer cell">\n          cancer cells\n         </a>\n         with nuclei (specifically the DNA) stained blue. The central and rightmost cell are in\n         <a href="/wiki/Interphase" title="Interphase">\n          interphase\n         </a>\n         , so the entire nuclei are labeled. The cell on the left is going through\n         <a href="/wiki/Mitosis" title="Mitosis">\n          mitosis\n         </a>\n         and its DNA has condensed.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_theory" title="Cell theory">\n        Cell theory\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cell theory states that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">\n        cell\n       </a>\n       is the fundamental unit of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       , that all living things are composed of one or more cells, and that all cells arise from other cells through\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_division" title="Cell division">\n        cell division\n       </a>\n       . In\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicellular_organisms" title="Multicellular organisms">\n        multicellular organisms\n       </a>\n       , every cell in the organism\'s body derives ultimately from a single cell in a fertilized\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egg_(biology)" title="Egg (biology)">\n        egg\n       </a>\n       . The cell is also considered to be the basic unit in many pathological processes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, the phenomenon of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_transfer" title="Energy transfer">\n        energy flow\n       </a>\n       occurs in cells in processes that are part of the function known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">\n        metabolism\n       </a>\n       . Finally, cells contain hereditary information (\n       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">\n        DNA\n       </a>\n       ), which is passed from cell to cell during cell division. Research into the origin of life,\n       <a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis">\n        abiogenesis\n       </a>\n       , amounts to an attempt to discover the origin of the first cells.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution">\n        Evolution\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg">\n         <img alt="diagram showing Natural selection favoring predominance of surviving mutation" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="331" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg/250px-Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg/375px-Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg/500px-Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mutation_and_selection_diagram.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">\n          Natural selection\n         </a>\n         of a population for dark coloration.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">\n        Evolution\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A central organizing concept in biology is that life changes and develops through evolution, and that all life-forms known have a\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_descent" title="Common descent">\n        common origin\n       </a>\n       . The theory of evolution postulates that all\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organisms\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       , both living and extinct, have descended from a common ancestor or an ancestral\n       <a href="/wiki/Gene_pool" title="Gene pool">\n        gene pool\n       </a>\n       . This\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_universal_common_ancestor_of_all_organisms" title="Last universal common ancestor of all organisms">\n        universal common ancestor of all organisms\n       </a>\n       is believed to have appeared about\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_evolution" title="Timeline of evolution">\n        3.5 billion years ago\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Biologists regard the ubiquity of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetic_code" title="Genetic code">\n        genetic code\n       </a>\n       as definitive evidence in favor of the theory of universal common descent for all\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">\n        bacteria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">\n        archaea\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">\n        eukaryotes\n       </a>\n       (see:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_life" title="Origin of life">\n        origin of life\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Futuyma_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Futuyma-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "evolution" was introduced into the scientific lexicon by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_de_Lamarck" title="Jean-Baptiste de Lamarck">\n        Jean-Baptiste de Lamarck\n       </a>\n       in 1809,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p15_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-p15-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and fifty years later\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">\n        Charles Darwin\n       </a>\n       posited a scientific model of natural selection as evolution\'s driving force.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Russel_Wallace" title="Alfred Russel Wallace">\n        Alfred Russel Wallace\n       </a>\n       is recognized as the co-discoverer of this concept as he helped research and experiment with the concept of evolution.)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Evolution is now used to explain the great variations of life found on Earth.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Darwin theorized that species flourish or die when subjected to the processes of\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">\n        natural selection\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a href="/wiki/Selective_breeding" title="Selective breeding">\n        selective breeding\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetic_drift" title="Genetic drift">\n        Genetic drift\n       </a>\n       was embraced as an additional mechanism of evolutionary development in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Modern_synthesis_(20th_century)" title="Modern synthesis (20th century)">\n        modern synthesis\n       </a>\n       of the theory.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GGS_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GGS-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The evolutionary history of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">\n        species\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94which describes the characteristics of the various species from which it descended\xe2\x80\x94together with its genealogical relationship to every other species is known as its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phylogeny" title="Phylogeny">\n        phylogeny\n       </a>\n       . Widely varied approaches to biology generate information about phylogeny. These include the comparisons of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DNA_sequence" title="DNA sequence">\n        DNA sequences\n       </a>\n       , a product of\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n        molecular biology\n       </a>\n       (more particularly\n       <a href="/wiki/Genomics" title="Genomics">\n        genomics\n       </a>\n       ), and comparisons of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">\n        fossils\n       </a>\n       or other records of ancient organisms, a product of\n       <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">\n        paleontology\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Biologists organize and analyze evolutionary relationships through various methods, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetics" title="Phylogenetics">\n        phylogenetics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Phenetics" title="Phenetics">\n        phenetics\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cladistics" title="Cladistics">\n        cladistics\n       </a>\n       . (For a summary of major events in the evolution of life as currently understood by biologists, see\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evolutionary_timeline" title="Evolutionary timeline">\n        evolutionary timeline\n       </a>\n       .)\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Evolution is relevant to the understanding of the natural history of life forms and to the understanding of the organization of current life forms. But, those organizations can only be understood in the light of how they came to be by way of the process of evolution. Consequently, evolution is central to all fields of biology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:right;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Genetics">\n        Genetics\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg">\n         <img alt="two by two table showing genetic crosses" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg/250px-Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg/375px-Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg/500px-Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Punnett_square_mendel_flowers.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Punnett_square" title="Punnett square">\n          Punnett square\n         </a>\n         depicting a cross between two pea plants heterozygous for purple (B) and white (b) blossoms\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">\n        Genetics\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">\n        Genes\n       </a>\n       are the primary units of inheritance in all organisms. A gene is a unit of\n       <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">\n        heredity\n       </a>\n       and corresponds to a region of\n       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">\n        DNA\n       </a>\n       that influences the form or function of an organism in specific ways. All organisms, from bacteria to animals, share the same basic machinery that copies and translates DNA into\n       <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">\n        proteins\n       </a>\n       . Cells\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcription_(genetics)" title="Transcription (genetics)">\n        transcribe\n       </a>\n       a DNA gene into an\n       <a href="/wiki/RNA" title="RNA">\n        RNA\n       </a>\n       version of the gene, and a\n       <a href="/wiki/Ribosome" title="Ribosome">\n        ribosome\n       </a>\n       then\n       <a href="/wiki/Translation_(biology)" title="Translation (biology)">\n        translates\n       </a>\n       the RNA into a sequence of\n       <a href="/wiki/Amino_acid" title="Amino acid">\n        amino acids\n       </a>\n       known as a protein. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetic_code" title="Genetic code">\n        translation code\n       </a>\n       from RNA codon to amino acid is the same for most organisms. For example, a sequence of DNA that codes for\n       <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">\n        insulin\n       </a>\n       in humans also codes for insulin when inserted into other organisms, such as plants.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       DNA is found as linear\n       <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">\n        chromosomes\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">\n        eukaryotes\n       </a>\n       , and circular chromosomes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Prokaryote" title="Prokaryote">\n        prokaryotes\n       </a>\n       . A chromosome is an organized structure consisting of\n       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">\n        DNA\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Histone" title="Histone">\n        histones\n       </a>\n       . The set of chromosomes in a cell and any other hereditary information found in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitochondria" title="Mitochondria">\n        mitochondria\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chloroplasts" title="Chloroplasts">\n        chloroplasts\n       </a>\n       , or other locations is collectively known as a cell\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Genome" title="Genome">\n        genome\n       </a>\n       . In eukaryotes, genomic DNA is localized in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_nucleus" title="Cell nucleus">\n        cell nucleus\n       </a>\n       , or with small amounts in\n       <a href="/wiki/Mitochondrion" title="Mitochondrion">\n        mitochondria\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Chloroplast" title="Chloroplast">\n        chloroplasts\n       </a>\n       . In prokaryotes, the DNA is held within an irregularly shaped body in the cytoplasm called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nucleoid" title="Nucleoid">\n        nucleoid\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The genetic information in a genome is held within genes, and the complete assemblage of this information in an organism is called its\n       <a href="/wiki/Genotype" title="Genotype">\n        genotype\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Homeostasis">\n        Homeostasis\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Homeostasis" title="Homeostasis">\n        Homeostasis\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg">\n         <img alt="diagram showing feedback loop of hormones" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="273" data-file-width="259" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg/220px-ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg/330px-ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg/440px-ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ACTH_Negative_Feedback.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Hypothalamus" title="Hypothalamus">\n          hypothalamus\n         </a>\n         secretes\n         <a href="/wiki/Corticotropin-releasing_hormone" title="Corticotropin-releasing hormone">\n          CRH\n         </a>\n         , which directs the\n         <a href="/wiki/Pituitary_gland" title="Pituitary gland">\n          pituitary gland\n         </a>\n         to secrete\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ACTH" title="ACTH">\n          ACTH\n         </a>\n         . In turn, ACTH directs the adrenal cortex to secrete\n         <a href="/wiki/Glucocorticoid" title="Glucocorticoid">\n          glucocorticoids\n         </a>\n         , such as\n         <a href="/wiki/Cortisol" title="Cortisol">\n          cortisol\n         </a>\n         . The GCs then reduce the rate of secretion by the hypothalamus and the pituitary gland once a sufficient amount of GCs has been released.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n          <a href="#cite_note-35">\n           [35]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Homeostasis is the ability of an\n       <a href="/wiki/Open_system_(systems_theory)" title="Open system (systems theory)">\n        open system\n       </a>\n       to regulate its internal environment to maintain stable conditions by means of multiple\n       <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_equilibrium" title="Dynamic equilibrium">\n        dynamic equilibrium\n       </a>\n       adjustments that are controlled by interrelated regulation mechanisms. All living\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organisms\n       </a>\n       , whether\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_celled" title="Single celled">\n        unicellular\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multicellular" title="Multicellular">\n        multicellular\n       </a>\n       , exhibit homeostasis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       To maintain dynamic equilibrium and effectively carry out certain functions, a system must detect and respond to perturbations. After the detection of a perturbation, a biological system normally responds through\n       <a href="/wiki/Negative_feedback" title="Negative feedback">\n        negative feedback\n       </a>\n       that stabilize conditions by reducing or increasing the activity of an organ or system. One example is the release of\n       <a href="/wiki/Glucagon" title="Glucagon">\n        glucagon\n       </a>\n       when sugar levels are too low.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Energy_and_life.svg">\n         <img alt="diagram showing human energy process from food input to heat and waste output" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="565" data-file-width="746" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Energy_and_life.svg/240px-Energy_and_life.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Energy_and_life.svg/360px-Energy_and_life.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Energy_and_life.svg/480px-Energy_and_life.svg.png 2x" width="240"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Energy_and_life.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Basic overview of\n         <a href="/wiki/Bioenergetics" title="Bioenergetics">\n          energy and human life\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">\n        Energy\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The survival of a living organism depends on the continuous input of\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       . Chemical reactions that are responsible for its structure and function are tuned to extract\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemistry#Energy" title="Chemistry">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       from substances that act as its food and transform them to help form new cells and sustain them. In this process,\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecules\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_substance" title="Chemical substance">\n        chemical substances\n       </a>\n       that constitute\n       <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">\n        food\n       </a>\n       play two roles; first, they contain energy that can be transformed and reused in that organism\'s biological,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_reaction" title="Chemical reaction">\n        chemical reactions\n       </a>\n       ; second, food can be transformed into new molecular structures (biomolecules) that are of use to that organism.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The organisms responsible for the introduction of energy into an ecosystem are known as producers or\n       <a href="/wiki/Autotroph" title="Autotroph">\n        autotrophs\n       </a>\n       . Nearly all such organisms originally draw their energy from the sun.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bryantfrigaard_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bryantfrigaard-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Plants and other\n       <a href="/wiki/Phototroph" title="Phototroph">\n        phototrophs\n       </a>\n       use solar energy via a process known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Photosynthesis" title="Photosynthesis">\n        photosynthesis\n       </a>\n       to convert raw materials into organic molecules, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Adenosine_triphosphate" title="Adenosine triphosphate">\n        ATP\n       </a>\n       , whose bonds can be broken to release energy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A few\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecosystems" title="Ecosystems">\n        ecosystems\n       </a>\n       , however, depend entirely on energy extracted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemotroph" title="Chemotroph">\n        chemotrophs\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">\n        methane\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sulfides" title="Sulfides">\n        sulfides\n       </a>\n       , or other non-\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">\n        luminal\n       </a>\n       energy sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some of the energy thus captured produces\n       <a href="/wiki/Biomass" title="Biomass">\n        biomass\n       </a>\n       and energy that is available for growth and development of other\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        life\n       </a>\n       forms. The majority of the rest of this biomass and energy are lost as waste molecules and heat. The most important processes for converting the energy trapped in chemical substances into energy useful to sustain life are\n       <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">\n        metabolism\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cellular_respiration" title="Cellular respiration">\n        cellular respiration\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Colvard.2C_2009_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Colvard.2C_2009-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Study_and_research">\n        Study and research\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Structural">\n        Structural\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n        Molecular biology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">\n        Cell biology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">\n        Genetics\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Developmental_biology" title="Developmental biology">\n        Developmental biology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biological_cell.svg">\n         <img alt="color diagram of cell as bowl" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="891" data-file-width="1466" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Biological_cell.svg/300px-Biological_cell.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Biological_cell.svg/450px-Biological_cell.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Biological_cell.svg/600px-Biological_cell.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biological_cell.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Schematic of typical animal\n         <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">\n          cell\n         </a>\n         depicting the various\n         <a href="/wiki/Organelle" title="Organelle">\n          organelles\n         </a>\n         and structures.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n        Molecular biology\n       </a>\n       is the study of biology at the molecular level.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This field overlaps with other areas of biology, particularly those of\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">\n        genetics\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n        biochemistry\n       </a>\n       . Molecular biology is a study of the interactions of the various systems within a cell, including the interrelationships of DNA, RNA, and protein synthesis and how those interactions are regulated.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The next larger scale,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">\n        cell biology\n       </a>\n       , studies the structural and\n       <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">\n        physiological\n       </a>\n       properties of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">\n        cells\n       </a>\n       , including their internal\n       <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">\n        behavior\n       </a>\n       , interactions with other cells, and with their\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">\n        environment\n       </a>\n       . This is done on both the\n       <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">\n        microscopic\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecular\n       </a>\n       levels, for unicellular organisms such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">\n        bacteria\n       </a>\n       , as well as the specialized cells of multicellular organisms such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">\n        humans\n       </a>\n       . Understanding the structure and function of cells is fundamental to all of the biological sciences. The similarities and differences between cell types are particularly relevant to molecular biology.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">\n        Anatomy\n       </a>\n       is a treatment of the macroscopic forms of such structures\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organ_(biology)" title="Organ (biology)">\n        organs\n       </a>\n       and organ systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">\n        Genetics\n       </a>\n       is the science of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">\n        genes\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Heredity" title="Heredity">\n        heredity\n       </a>\n       , and the variation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organisms\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-griffiths2000sect60_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-griffiths2000sect60-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hartl_and_Jones_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hartl_and_Jones-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Genes encode the information needed by cells for the synthesis of proteins, which in turn play a central role in influencing the final\n       <a href="/wiki/Phenotype" title="Phenotype">\n        phenotype\n       </a>\n       of the organism. Genetics provides research tools used in the investigation of the function of a particular gene, or the analysis of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_interaction" title="Genetic interaction">\n        genetic interactions\n       </a>\n       . Within organisms, genetic information is physically represented as\n       <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">\n        chromosomes\n       </a>\n       , within which it is represented by a particular\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DNA_sequence" title="DNA sequence">\n        sequence\n       </a>\n       of amino acids in particular\n       <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">\n        DNA\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Molecule" title="Molecule">\n        molecules\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Developmental_biology" title="Developmental biology">\n        Developmental biology\n       </a>\n       studies the process by which organisms grow and develop. Developmental biology, originated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Embryology" title="Embryology">\n        embryology\n       </a>\n       , studies the genetic control of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_growth" title="Cell growth">\n        cell growth\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cellular_differentiation" title="Cellular differentiation">\n        cellular differentiation\n       </a>\n       , and "cellular\n       <a href="/wiki/Morphogenesis" title="Morphogenesis">\n        morphogenesis\n       </a>\n       ," which is the process that progressively gives rise to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_tissue" title="Biological tissue">\n        tissues\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">\n        organs\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">\n        anatomy\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Model_organism" title="Model organism">\n        Model organisms\n       </a>\n       for developmental biology include the round worm\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Caenorhabditis_elegans" title="Caenorhabditis elegans">\n         Caenorhabditis elegans\n        </a>\n        ,\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the fruit fly\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Drosophila_melanogaster" title="Drosophila melanogaster">\n         Drosophila melanogaster\n        </a>\n        ,\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_genetics_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_genetics-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the zebrafish\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danio_rerio" title="Danio rerio">\n         Danio rerio\n        </a>\n        ,\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the mouse\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mus_musculus" title="Mus musculus">\n         Mus musculus\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the weed\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Arabidopsis_thaliana" title="Arabidopsis thaliana">\n         Arabidopsis thaliana\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (A model organism is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">\n        species\n       </a>\n       that is extensively studied to understand particular biological\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phenomena" title="Phenomena">\n        phenomena\n       </a>\n       , with the expectation that discoveries made in that organism provide insight into the workings of other organisms.)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physiological">\n        Physiological\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">\n        Physiology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Physiology is the study of the mechanical, physical, and biochemical processes of living organisms function as a whole. The theme of "structure to function" is central to biology. Physiological studies have traditionally been divided into\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant_physiology" title="Plant physiology">\n        plant physiology\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animal_physiology" title="Animal physiology">\n        animal physiology\n       </a>\n       , but some principles of physiology are universal, no matter what particular\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organism\n       </a>\n       is being studied. For example, what is learned about the physiology of\n       <a href="/wiki/Yeast" title="Yeast">\n        yeast\n       </a>\n       cells can also apply to human cells. The field of animal physiology extends the tools and methods of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_physiology" title="Human physiology">\n        human physiology\n       </a>\n       to non-human species. Plant physiology borrows techniques from both research fields.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Physiology is the study the interaction of how, for example, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nervous_system" title="Nervous system">\n        nervous\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Immune_system" title="Immune system">\n        immune\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Endocrine_system" title="Endocrine system">\n        endocrine\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Respiratory_system" title="Respiratory system">\n        respiratory\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Circulatory_system" title="Circulatory system">\n        circulatory\n       </a>\n       systems, function and interact. The study of these systems is shared with such\n       <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">\n        medically\n       </a>\n       oriented disciplines as\n       <a href="/wiki/Neurology" title="Neurology">\n        neurology\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Immunology" title="Immunology">\n        immunology\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolutionary">\n        Evolutionary\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Current_research_in_evolutionary_biology" title="Current research in evolutionary biology">\n        Evolutionary research\n       </a>\n       is concerned with the origin and descent of\n       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">\n        species\n       </a>\n       , and their change over time. It employs scientists from many taxonomically oriented disciplines, for example, those with special training in particular\n       <a href="/wiki/Organism" title="Organism">\n        organisms\n       </a>\n       such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Mammalogy" title="Mammalogy">\n        mammalogy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ornithology" title="Ornithology">\n        ornithology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">\n        botany\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Herpetology" title="Herpetology">\n        herpetology\n       </a>\n       , but are of use in answering more general questions about evolution.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Evolutionary biology is partly based on\n       <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">\n        paleontology\n       </a>\n       , which uses the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fossil" title="Fossil">\n        fossil\n       </a>\n       record to answer questions about the mode and tempo of evolution,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jablonski_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Jablonski-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and partly on the developments in areas such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_genetics" title="Population genetics">\n        population genetics\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 1980s,\n       <a href="/wiki/Developmental_biology" title="Developmental biology">\n        developmental biology\n       </a>\n       re-entered evolutionary biology after its initial exclusion from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Modern_synthesis_(20th_century)" title="Modern synthesis (20th century)">\n        modern synthesis\n       </a>\n       through the study of\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_developmental_biology" title="Evolutionary developmental biology">\n        evolutionary developmental biology\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetics" title="Phylogenetics">\n        Phylogenetics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Systematics" title="Systematics">\n        systematics\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alpha_taxonomy" title="Alpha taxonomy">\n        taxonomy\n       </a>\n       are related fields often considered part of evolutionary biology.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Systematic">\n        Systematic\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">\n        <div class="noresize">\n         <map id="ImageMap_1_645933365" name="ImageMap_1_645933365">\n          <area alt="Bacteria" coords="63,61,124,72" href="/wiki/Bacteria"   <area alt="Bacteroides" coords="7,200,56,209" href="/wiki/Bacteroides" shape="rect" title="Bacteroides"/>\n          <area alt="Bacteroides-Cytophaga" coords="57,201,97,214" <area alt="Thermococcus celer" coords="202,165,232,172" href="/wiki/Thermococci" shape="rect" title="Thermococcus celer"/>\n          <area alt="Methanococcus" coords="176,150,242,157"         <area alt="Methanosarcina" coords="202,125,269,132" href="/wiki/Methanosarcina" shape="rect" title="Methanosarcina"/>\n          <area alt="Halophiles" coords="269,136,312,145"
