href="/wiki/Flagellate" shape="rect" title="Flagellate"/>\n          <area alt="Trichomonad" coords="382,201,441,208" href="/wiki/Trichomonad" shape="rect" title="Trichomonad"/>\n          <area alt="Microsporidia" coords="382,219,438,229" href="/wiki/Microsporidia" shape="rect" title="Microsporidia"/>\n          <area alt="Diplomonad" coords="382,241,436,250" href="/wiki/Diplomonad" shape="rect" title="Diplomonad"/>\n         </map>\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1250" data-file-width="1850" height="304" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Phylogenetic_tree.svg/450px-Phylogenetic_tree.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Phylogenetic_tree.svg/675px-Phylogenetic_tree.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Phylogenetic_tree.svg/900px-Phylogenetic_tree.svg.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_1_645933365" width="450"/>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phylogenetic_tree.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Phylogenetic_tree" title="Phylogenetic tree">\n          phylogenetic tree\n         </a>\n         of all living things, based on\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RRNA" title="RRNA">\n          rRNA\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Gene" title="Gene">\n          gene\n         </a>\n         data, showing the separation of the three domains\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">\n          bacteria\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">\n          archaea\n         </a>\n         , and\n         <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">\n          eukaryotes\n         </a>\n         as described initially by\n         <a href="/wiki/Carl_Woese" title="Carl Woese">\n          Carl Woese\n         </a>\n         . Trees constructed with other genes are generally similar, although they may place some early-branching groups very differently, presumably owing to rapid rRNA evolution. The exact relationships of the three domains are still being debated.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg">\n         <img alt="color diagram of taxonomy" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="230" height="564" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg/220px-Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg/330px-Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg/440px-Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Biological_classification_L_Pengo.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The hierarchy of\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biological_classification" title="Biological classification">\n          biological classification\n         </a>\n         \'s eight major taxonomic ranks. Intermediate minor rankings are not shown. This diagram uses a 3\n         <a href="/wiki/Domain_(biology)" title="Domain (biology)">\n          Domains\n         </a>\n         / 6\n         <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)" title="Kingdom (biology)">\n          Kingdoms\n         </a>\n         format\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Systematics" title="Systematics">\n        Systematics\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Multiple\n       <a href="/wiki/Speciation" title="Speciation">\n        speciation\n       </a>\n       events create a tree structured system of relationships between species. The role of\n       <a href="/wiki/Systematics" title="Systematics">\n        systematics\n       </a>\n       is to study these relationships and thus the differences and similarities between species and groups of species.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, systematics was an active field of research long before evolutionary thinking was common.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Traditionally, living things have been divided into five kingdoms:\n       <a href="/wiki/Monera" title="Monera">\n        Monera\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Protist" title="Protist">\n        Protista\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">\n        Fungi\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">\n        Plantae\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">\n        Animalia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, many scientists now consider this five-kingdom system outdated. Modern alternative classification systems generally begin with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Three-domain_system" title="Three-domain system">\n        three-domain system\n       </a>\n       :\n       <a href="/wiki/Archaea" title="Archaea">\n        Archaea\n       </a>\n       (originally Archaebacteria);\n       <a href="/wiki/Bacteria" title="Bacteria">\n        Bacteria\n       </a>\n       (originally Eubacteria) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Eukaryote" title="Eukaryote">\n        Eukaryota\n       </a>\n       (including\n       <a href="/wiki/Protist" title="Protist">\n        protists\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">\n        fungi\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plants" title="Plants">\n        plants\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Animal" title="Animal">\n        animals\n       </a>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domain_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-domain-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These domains reflect whether the cells have nuclei or not, as well as differences in the chemical composition of key biomolecules such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Ribosome" title="Ribosome">\n        ribosomes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-domain_59-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-domain-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Further, each kingdom is broken down recursively until each species is separately classified. The order is:\n       <a href="/wiki/Domain_(biology)" title="Domain (biology)">\n        Domain\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)" title="Kingdom (biology)">\n        Kingdom\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">\n        Phylum\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Class_(biology)" title="Class (biology)">\n        Class\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Order_(biology)" title="Order (biology)">\n        Order\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Family_(biology)" title="Family (biology)">\n        Family\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">\n        Genus\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">\n        Species\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Outside of these categories, there are obligate intracellular\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">\n        parasites\n       </a>\n       that are "on the edge of life"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in terms of\n       <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">\n        metabolic\n       </a>\n       activity, meaning that many scientists do not actually classify such structures as alive, due to their lack of at least one or more of the fundamental functions or characteristics that define life. They are classified as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virus_(biology)" title="Virus (biology)">\n        viruses\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Viroid" title="Viroid">\n        viroids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Prion" title="Prion">\n        prions\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_(biology)" title="Satellite (biology)">\n        satellites\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The scientific name of an organism is generated from its genus and species. For example, humans are listed as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">\n         Homo sapiens\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <i>\n        Homo\n       </i>\n       is the genus, and\n       <i>\n        sapiens\n       </i>\n       the species. When writing the scientific name of an organism, it is proper to capitalize the first letter in the genus and put all of the species in lowercase.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, the entire term may be italicized or underlined.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The dominant classification system is called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Linnaean_taxonomy" title="Linnaean taxonomy">\n        Linnaean taxonomy\n       </a>\n       . It includes ranks and\n       <a href="/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature" title="Binomial nomenclature">\n        binomial nomenclature\n       </a>\n       . How organisms are named is governed by international agreements such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Code_of_Nomenclature_for_algae,_fungi,_and_plants" title="International Code of Nomenclature for algae, fungi, and plants">\n        International Code of Nomenclature for algae, fungi, and plants\n       </a>\n       (ICN), the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Code_of_Zoological_Nomenclature" title="International Code of Zoological Nomenclature">\n        International Code of Zoological Nomenclature\n       </a>\n       (ICZN), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Code_of_Nomenclature_of_Bacteria" title="International Code of Nomenclature of Bacteria">\n        International Code of Nomenclature of Bacteria\n       </a>\n       (ICNB). The classification of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viruses" title="Viruses">\n        viruses\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viroids" title="Viroids">\n        viroids\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prions" title="Prions">\n        prions\n       </a>\n       , and all other sub-viral agents that demonstrate biological characteristics is conducted by the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Taxonomy_of_Viruses" title="International Committee on Taxonomy of Viruses">\n        International Committee on Taxonomy of Viruses\n       </a>\n       (ICTV) and is known as the International Code of Viral Classification and Nomenclature (ICVCN).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ictvdbpopsi_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ictvdbpopsi-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ictvdbprions_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ictvdbprions-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ictvdbsatel_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ictvdbsatel-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, several other viral classification systems do exist.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A merging draft,\n       <a href="/wiki/BioCode" title="BioCode">\n        BioCode\n       </a>\n       , was published in 1997 in an attempt to standardize nomenclature in these three areas, but has yet to be formally adopted.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The BioCode draft has received little attention since 1997; its originally planned implementation date of January 1, 2000, has passed unnoticed. A revised BioCode that, instead of replacing the existing codes, would provide a unified context for them, was proposed in 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Botanical_Congress" title="International Botanical Congress">\n        International Botanical Congress\n       </a>\n       of 2011 declined to consider the BioCode proposal. The\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Committee_on_Taxonomy_of_Viruses" title="International Committee on Taxonomy of Viruses">\n        ICVCN\n       </a>\n       remains outside the BioCode, which does not include viral classification.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdoms">\n        Kingdoms\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_(biology)" title="Kingdom (biology)">\n        Kingdom (biology)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <ul      <p>\n           <a href="/wiki/Virus" title="Virus">\n            Virus\n           </a>\n           \xe2\x80\x93 Gamma\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phage" title="Phage">\n            phage\n           </a>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_and_environmental">\n        Ecological and environmental\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Common_clownfish.jpg">\n         <img alt="a colorful cloudfish swimming near a sea anemone" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Common_clownfish.jpg/250px-Common_clownfish.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Common_clownfish.jpg/375px-Common_clownfish.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Common_clownfish.jpg/500px-Common_clownfish.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Common_clownfish.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Mutual\n         <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">\n          symbiosis\n         </a>\n         between\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clownfish" title="Clownfish">\n          clownfish\n         </a>\n         of the genus\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amphiprion" title="Amphiprion">\n          Amphiprion\n         </a>\n         that dwell among the tentacles of tropical\n         <a href="/wiki/Sea_anemone" title="Sea anemone">\n          sea anemones\n         </a>\n         . The territorial fish protects the anemone from anemone-eating fish, and in turn the stinging tentacles of the anemone protects the clown fish from its predators.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">\n        Ecology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">\n        Ethology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">\n        Behavior\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">\n        Biogeography\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">\n        Ecology\n       </a>\n       is the study of the distribution and abundance of\n       <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">\n        living organisms\n       </a>\n       , the interaction between them and their\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">\n        environment\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An organism shares an environment that includes other organisms and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biotic_factors" title="Biotic factors">\n        biotic factors\n       </a>\n       as well as local\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abiotic_factors" title="Abiotic factors">\n        abiotic factors\n       </a>\n       (non-living) such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">\n        climate\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">\n        ecology\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-habitats_of_the_world_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-habitats_of_the_world-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One reason that biological systems can be difficult to study is that so many different interactions with other organisms and the environment are possible, even on small scales. A microscopic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">\n        bacterium\n       </a>\n       responding to a local sugar gradient is responding to its environment as much as a lion searching for food in the African\n       <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">\n        savanna\n       </a>\n       . For any species,\n       <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">\n        behaviors\n       </a>\n       can be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Co-operation" title="Co-operation">\n        co-operative\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Competition_(biology)" title="Competition (biology)">\n        competitive\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parasite" title="Parasite">\n        parasitic\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a href="/wiki/Symbiosis" title="Symbiosis">\n        symbiotic\n       </a>\n       . Matters become more complex when two or more species interact in an\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">\n        ecosystem\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ecological systems are studied at several different levels, from the scale of the ecology of individual organisms, to those of\n       <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">\n        populations\n       </a>\n       , to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">\n        ecosystems\n       </a>\n       and finally the\n       <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">\n        biosphere\n       </a>\n       . The term\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Population_biology" title="Population biology">\n        population biology\n       </a>\n       is often used interchangeably with\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_ecology" title="Population ecology">\n        population ecology\n       </a>\n       , although\n       <i>\n        population biology\n       </i>\n       is more frequently used in the case of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diseases" title="Diseases">\n        diseases\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viruses" title="Viruses">\n        viruses\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microbes" title="Microbes">\n        microbes\n       </a>\n       , while the term population ecology is more commonly applied to the study of plants and animals. Ecology draws on many subdisciplines.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">\n        Ethology\n       </a>\n       is the study of animal\n       <a href="/wiki/Behavior" title="Behavior">\n        behavior\n       </a>\n       (particularly that of social animals such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Primate" title="Primate">\n        primates\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Canidae" title="Canidae">\n        canids\n       </a>\n       ), and is sometimes considered a branch of zoology. Ethologists have been particularly concerned with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">\n        evolution\n       </a>\n       of behavior and the understanding of behavior in terms of the theory of\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">\n        natural selection\n       </a>\n       . In one sense, the first modern ethologist was\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">\n        Charles Darwin\n       </a>\n       , whose book,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Expression_of_the_Emotions_in_Man_and_Animals" title="The Expression of the Emotions in Man and Animals">\n         The Expression of the Emotions in Man and Animals\n        </a>\n        ,\n       </i>\n       influenced many ethologists to come.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-black_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-black-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">\n        Biogeography\n       </a>\n       studies the spatial distribution of organisms on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">\n        Earth\n       </a>\n       , focusing on such topics as\n       <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">\n        plate tectonics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        climate change\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Biological_dispersal" title="Biological dispersal">\n        dispersal\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Animal_migration" title="Animal migration">\n        migration\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cladistics" title="Cladistics">\n        cladistics\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_unresolved_problems_in_biology">\n        Basic unresolved problems in biology\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_unsolved_problems_in_biology" title="List of unsolved problems in biology">\n        List of unsolved problems in biology\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Despite the profound advances made over recent decades in our understanding of life\'s fundamental processes, some basic problems have remained unresolved. One of the major unresolved problems in biology is the primary adaptive function of sex, and particularly its key processes in eukaryotes of meiosis and homologous recombination. One view is that sex evolved primarily as an adaptation that promoted increased genetic diversity (see references e.g.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ). An alternative view is that sex is an adaptation for promoting accurate DNA repair in germ-line DNA, and that increased genetic diversity is primarily a byproduct that may be useful in the long run.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (See also\n       <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_sexual_reproduction" title="Evolution of sexual reproduction">\n        Evolution of sexual reproduction\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another basic unresolved problem in biology is the biologic basis of aging. At present, there is no consensus view on the underlying cause of aging. Various competing theories are outlined in\n       <a href="/wiki/Ageing#Theories" title="Ageing">\n        Ageing Theories\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Branches">\n        Branches\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       These are the main branches of biology:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For a more detailed list, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_biology" title="Outline of biology">\n        outline of biology\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Aerobiology" title="Aerobiology">\n         Aerobiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of airborne organic particles\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">\n         Agriculture\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of producing crops and raising livestock, with an emphasis on practical applications\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Anatomy" title="Anatomy">\n         Anatomy\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of form and function, in plants, animals, and other organisms, or specifically in humans\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Histology" title="Histology">\n           Histology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of cells and tissues, a microscopic branch of anatomy\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">\n         Astrobiology\n        </a>\n        (also known as exobiology, exopaleontology, and bioastronomy) \xe2\x80\x93 the study of evolution, distribution, and future of life in the universe\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n         Biochemistry\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chemical_reactions" title="Chemical reactions">\n         chemical reactions\n        </a>\n        required for life to exist and function, usually a focus on the cellular level\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bioengineering" title="Bioengineering">\n         Bioengineering\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of biology through the means of engineering with an emphasis on applied knowledge and especially related to biotechnology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">\n         Biogeography\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the distribution of species spatially and temporally\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Bioinformatics" title="Bioinformatics">\n         Bioinformatics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the use of information technology for the study, collection, and storage of genomic and other biological data\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biolinguistics" title="Biolinguistics">\n         Biolinguistics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the biology and evolution of language.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomathematics" title="Biomathematics">\n         Biomathematics\n        </a>\n        (or Mathematical biology) \xe2\x80\x93 the quantitative or mathematical study of biological processes, with an emphasis on modeling\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biomechanics" title="Biomechanics">\n         Biomechanics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the mechanics of living beings\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_research" title="Biomedical research">\n         Biomedical research\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of health and disease\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Pharmacology" title="Pharmacology">\n           Pharmacology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study and practical application of preparation, use, and effects of drugs and synthetic medicines\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biomusicology" title="Biomusicology">\n         Biomusicology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of music from a biological point of view.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">\n         Biophysics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of biological processes through physics, by applying the theories and methods traditionally used in the physical sciences\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biosemiotics" title="Biosemiotics">\n         Biosemiotics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of biological processes through\n        <a href="/wiki/Semiotics" title="Semiotics">\n         semiotics\n        </a>\n        , by applying the models of meaning-making and communication\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">\n         Biotechnology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the manipulation of living matter, including genetic modification and\n        <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_biology" title="Synthetic biology">\n         synthetic biology\n        </a>\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_biology" title="Synthetic biology">\n           Synthetic biology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 research integrating biology and engineering; construction of biological functions not found in nature\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Building_biology" title="Building biology">\n         Building biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the indoor living environment\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">\n         Botany\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of plants\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">\n         Cell biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the cell as a complete unit, and the molecular and chemical interactions that occur within a living cell\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_biology" title="Cognitive biology">\n         Cognitive biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of\n        <a href="/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">\n         cognition\n        </a>\n        as a biological function\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">\n         Conservation biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the preservation, protection, or restoration of the natural environment, natural ecosystems, vegetation, and wildlife\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Cryobiology" title="Cryobiology">\n         Cryobiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the effects of lower than normally preferred temperatures on living beings\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Developmental_biology" title="Developmental biology">\n         Developmental biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the processes through which an organism forms, from zygote to full structure\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Embryology" title="Embryology">\n           Embryology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the development of embryo (from fecundation to birth)\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">\n         Ecology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the interactions of living organisms with one another and with the non-living elements of their environment\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_biology" title="Environmental biology">\n         Environmental biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the natural world, as a whole or in a particular area, especially as affected by human activity\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Epidemiology" title="Epidemiology">\n         Epidemiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 a major component of public health research, studying factors affecting the health of populations\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Evolutionary_biology" title="Evolutionary biology">\n         Evolutionary biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the origin and descent of species over time\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">\n         Genetics\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of genes and heredity.\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Epigenetics" title="Epigenetics">\n           Epigenetics\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of heritable changes in gene expression or cellular phenotype caused by mechanisms other than changes in the underlying DNA sequence\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hematology" title="Hematology">\n         Hematology\n        </a>\n        (also known as Haematology) \xe2\x80\x93 the study of blood and blood-forming organs.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrative_biology" title="Integrative biology">\n         Integrative biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of whole organisms\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Limnology" title="Limnology">\n         Limnology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of inland waters\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Marine_biology" title="Marine biology">\n         Marine biology\n        </a>\n        (or biological oceanography) \xe2\x80\x93 the study of ocean ecosystems, plants, animals, and other living beings\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Microbiology" title="Microbiology">\n         Microbiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of microscopic organisms (microorganisms) and their interactions with other living things\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Bacteriology" title="Bacteriology">\n           Bacteriology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of bacteria\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Mycology" title="Mycology">\n           Mycology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of fungi\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Parasitology" title="Parasitology">\n           Parasitology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of parasites and parasitism\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Virology" title="Virology">\n           Virology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of viruses and some other virus-like agents\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n         Molecular biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of biology and biological functions at the molecular level, some cross over with biochemistry\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanobiology" title="Nanobiology">\n         Nanobiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of how\n        <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">\n         nanotechnology\n        </a>\n        can be used in biology, and the study of living organisms and parts on the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanoscale" title="Nanoscale">\n         nanoscale\n        </a>\n        level of organization\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">\n         Neuroscience\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the nervous system, including anatomy, physiology and pathology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Population_biology" title="Population biology">\n         Population biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of groups of conspecific organisms, including\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Population_ecology" title="Population ecology">\n           Population ecology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of how population dynamics and extinction\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Population_genetics" title="Population genetics">\n           Population genetics\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of changes in gene frequencies in populations of organisms\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">\n         Paleontology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of fossils and sometimes geographic evidence of prehistoric life\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pathology" title="Pathology">\n         Pathobiology or pathology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of diseases, and the causes, processes, nature, and development of disease\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">\n         Physiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the functioning of living organisms and the organs and parts of living organisms\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phytopathology" title="Phytopathology">\n         Phytopathology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of plant diseases (also called Plant Pathology)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychobiology" title="Psychobiology">\n         Psychobiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the biological bases of\n        <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">\n         psychology\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_biology" title="Quantum biology">\n         Quantum biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of\n        <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">\n         quantum mechanics\n        </a>\n        to biological objects and problems.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Sociobiology" title="Sociobiology">\n         Sociobiology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of the biological bases of\n        <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">\n         sociology\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Structural_biology" title="Structural biology">\n         Structural biology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 a branch of\n        <a href="/wiki/Molecular_biology" title="Molecular biology">\n         molecular biology\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">\n         biochemistry\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Biophysics" title="Biophysics">\n         biophysics\n        </a>\n        concerned with the molecular structure of biological macromolecules\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Zoology" title="Zoology">\n         Zoology\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the study of animals, including classification, physiology, development, and behavior, including:\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Ethology" title="Ethology">\n           Ethology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of animal behavior\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Entomology" title="Entomology">\n           Entomology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of insects\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Herpetology" title="Herpetology">\n           Herpetology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of reptiles and amphibians\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Ichthyology" title="Ichthyology">\n           Ichthyology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of fish\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Mammalogy" title="Mammalogy">\n           Mammalogy\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of mammals\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Ornithology" title="Ornithology">\n           Ornithology\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 the study of birds\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="metadata mbox-small"
